<Author>razvanl
<Content>No way Jose! We ended up booking a one week stay with this hotel in Madrid, after reviewing comments on tripadvisor.com. As for the decorations, the glamor from the photos is lost, as the nice painted walls just look fade and colorless. The bathroom is actually just a small closet, fitted with a shower cabin and toilet - it had the smallest sink I ever saw and the economic shower head, that pumps water under pressure, great on the environment but absolutely dreadful when it comes to taking a proper shower in less then 30 minutes.Breakfast was not that bad, so that's a plus. However, being located next to the breakfast area meant we invariably had to wake up when the first guests arrived for breakfast - don't ask about the Don't disturb sign, is just that, a sign.I guess we just clinched our teeth and did not leave earlier because we just did not want to let this ruin our beautiful experience in Madrid. Guess that will not happen next time, because there will not be a next stay at this hotel.Adios!

<Author>Ava1512
<Content>Nice but over-rated Took a shine to Mario when I saw the pictures on its official website; the rooms looked incredibly stylish. Truth was while the hotel lobby was very chic and decked out in designer furnishings, the room we stayed in was less than impressive. Firstly, it was way smaller than we had expected, especially the bathroom or should I say shower-area? It was literally that; a shower space in a glass case right next to the toilet seat. The basin was situated out of the bathroom because there just wasn't any space!Add to that, the water in the shower just would not drain! So if you keep the shower turned on, you'll soon be flooded. Plus, water was flowing out through the glass door which wasn't properly built to shut. At the end of it all, there was water on the floor outside the shower which in turn soaked through the bathmat/towel meant to dry your feet and keep them toasty after a hot shower.Next came the beddings. I found strands of hair on the white sheets! Unacceptable for a mid-range hotel that prides itself on being a designer-boutique brandname.The only saving grace was the very helpful assistance we received from one of the staff, Guido. We needed directions to get to a shopping outlet located outside of Madrid. Guido spent more than 20mins giving us detailed directions, pointing out the Metro stops on the map, checking the exact address of the outlet on the internet and providing personal recommendations. Definitely went beyond his call of duty! Thank you Guido.Overall, while the hotel experience was mediocre, its location was good; you're less than a minute's walk away from the Metro (Opera) and about 15mins walk from the major shopping belt; Gran Via. There is also the lovely Teatro Real right next door. Other than that, Mario should seriously consider looking into improving their room standards if they would like to keep up with the competition.

<Author>kinderkinder
<Content>very good location We spent 4 days in Madrid with a friend from 14 til 18 of November in Mario hotel.The hotel is very good located in the centre of Madrid at metro station Opera. But if you are coming from the airport (as we were)- it is not really very convenient by metro because you have to change the lines twice- so you are going by 3 different metro lines. It takes not so much time but actually we came to Madrid on Friday about 16 PM and it was a great crowd in metro. So we passed through some trains but all of them were full, so we got inside with great problems and decided to go to the airport for our coming back by taxi. I can say that it costed us 40 eur by taxi. I would say much more expencive than we were expecting... The guy at the reception told us it should cost about 25 eur. But we had our taxi early in the morning (about 5:30) and we had Terminal 4, that is the most far situated. May be that was the reason of the high price.About the hotel.... By hotel graduation it has 2 stars superior. It has nice desigh. Of course all the desigh is made from not expencive materials but anyway it looks good. We had standart room in white colors. Two twin beds. And the window looking to the inside. So its not even yard view- its just small space between four walls. But we didnt mind- we had all the time blind closed. The bathroom with a bath. Safe box in the room. Big wardrobe. We were thinking we had not big mirror in the room- only one we had in the bathroom, but at the last day we recognized its inside the wardrobe on the door:)Little LDC tv, i would say too little for watching, its like a pc display. But we only were listening to music channels so it wasnt a problem for us...Every day after cleaning we found green apple on the bedside table- very pleasant surprise:)Individual thanks to cleaning lady (if i dont make mistake her name is Esther)- she is so sunny, nice, allways smiling person.The breakfats is served till 12:00- good enough- cheese, ham, toasts, musli, yogurts, spanish tortilla.Sometimes we were lost in hotels corridors, but its not so difficult as it could seem from the first time...Sometimes when we were relaxing before dinner it was rather loud for sleeping, but in the morning time- no claim.The reception very helpful, answering all the questions.Also there is a PC in the corner so you can check your mail if you need- no fee.The location of the hotel is great- centre. So we didnt use public transport at all- all the time walking around on foot. One day we took city bus tour- it cost appr.16 eur for one day, 20 eur for two days. its very nice to see all the sightseeings- and you can hop on hop off during all the day...We booked the hotel on the hotels website and we got special offer- stay 4 nights with Mario. It costed us 470 eur- 4 days for 2 people. So very nice design hotel at the very good centre location with late breakfasts till 12:00 and helpful staff.

<Author>Belgian_EU
<Content>Good hotel in good location We stayed in the Room Mate Mario for four nights at the end of October 2008. Having stayed there once before and been impressed, booked again for another stay.Prices were high for the holiday week so we had booked an ordinary room. The first room offered had a view to the outside, but the windows did not properly shut. The hotel immediately came to check, verified that the window would not shut, and so promptly showed me two other rooms, one of which I accepted. Gracias, Samuel, for being so efficient.The room was rather stuffy as the weather had been good for a couple of days, but the aircon had been moved to 'heat'. However as the windows opened, this was not a problem.The room was small, but well-apportioned, with a generous wardrobe, cupboards, large bed, small flat screen TV and large bathroom with shower.Free internet was in the room with a password from reception, and the hotel was happy to print our boarding passes for us.Breakfast was included and huge, and included soya milk and a large selection of cold breakfast things.Location is perfect, on a quiet street just minutes from Opera metro station but a short walk to Gran Via, restaurants, bars and the Chueca area.

<Author>EmilyLang
<Content>Great location Considering this is a 2 star property I was pleasantly surprised. First of all, the location on Calle Campomanes is excellent. And the first impression of the hotel is great: The lobby is minimalistic and chic and very very cool. The people at the front desk were always nice and helpful, and - compared to the rest of the city - spoke great English.Our room (117) was located on the first floor, facing the street. The Madrilenos are talkative and loud people, particularly when they've had a couple of drinks, but that's about the only noise we experienced from the otherwise quiet street (Calle Campomanes). The rooms are minimalistic and quite small, with an interesting en suite bathroom. Basically the shower and the toilet is in the same room as the bed, only hidden by a glass door. If you're sensitive to those kinds of sounds, you should probably find someplace else to stay... The sink and the mirror is however placed outside these glass walls right in front of the bed, which I found nice as I could put on my make-up (although the lighting was not too good) and get ready while my boyfriend was taking a shower. Our room was conveniently located only a few feet away from the breakfast area, but this also proved to be negative as there was quite a bit of noise in the early mornings. I believe rooms 116, 117 and 118 are the only rooms affected by this - so my advise would be to ask to switch if you get one of these three.The breakfast itself was excellent though. It's the continental type, which means you have a buffet to choose from. The Spanish potato omelette is highly recommended ;)Also, kudos for free wi-fi in all rooms!

<Author>Elyse1316
<Content>Mario Did the Job Mario is nicely located within a couple blocks of the Royal Palace and a 5 minute walk to Plaza Mayor and Puerta de Sol. The Room Mate hotel chain seems to be opening new properties which were booked at the time we planned our trip. Mario was one of the only properties left as we would have liked a newer property such as Oscar. Our room was clean and nicely sized facing the street with a small balcony. Noise was not an issue for us as the windows did a great job of blocking out sound. We were only a couple floors off the street and didn't hear a peep. The hotel isn't on a main street, so it was relatively quiet anyway.The hotel delivered what was expected, but showed signs of wear and tear. Breakfast was included in the rate and was a nice selection of fruits, breads, meats, cheeses, tortillas (spanish egg and potato omelette), and cereals.The staff was very friendly and helpful and spoke great English. Free online access in the lobby helped us build our game plan for our nights out in the city.I would stay at the Mario again, however, would probably try to stay at a newer property.

<Author>patatasbravas
<Content>Mucho mas que Mario! The Room Mate Mario is diagonally opposite the Opera metro exit, across the plaza, and slightly uphill on c/ Campomanes. From the minute we stepped in, we were blown away by the hotel. Funky decor, reading area, free internet - that's just within the first 10 metres!Reception, at check-in, recommended a street-facing room (the views were nicer) so we agreed. Got to our room, and were extremely impressed. For North Americans, the room would have seemed slightly compact, but all the facilities needed were there. Plasma screen TV (only one English-speaking channel though), mini-bar (with space for storing your own items, much appreciated), digital safe, fully functioning bathroom with insane power shower, an expansive double bed, a small balcony and free apples each day!!! The breakfast, provided as part of the room price, was more than substantial. No greasy bacon and eggs, which was no shame, but croissants, cooked meats, fruits, cake, yoghurts, juices and coffees on tap. Mario is just a short walk from the Palacio RèŒ…al, Plaza Mayor and the Puerta del Sol and Madrid's base for many, many bars, cafèŒ…s and eateries. Access from the airport involved 2 changes on the metro (we used line 8 to Nuevos Ministerios, then line 10 to Alonso Martinez, followed by line 5 to Opera).We highly recommended the hotel to young people or couples of any age looking for a chilled-out, trendy and good value hotel base in Madrid.

<Author>fickle-traveller
<Content>Perfect for a visit to Madrid We really enjoyed our three night stay at the Mario. The rooms are small but adequate and, like the rest of the hotel, spotlessly clean. For us, the best points were the central location in a quiet street, the excellent breakfast and the friendly staff.Our room was at the back of the hotel, with a tiny window and no views but the compensation was the quietness, apart from some inconsiderate corridor noise. We had no problems with the bathroom which actually had a (very welcome) bath in it.Our favourite place to eat was the Museo del Jamon in Calle Mayor, where you can stand at the counter with the crowd of locals and have a drink and a sandwich or eat a hot meal upstairs in the equally packed cafeteria. Great atmosphere and reasonable prices.For a full restaurant meal, try La Vaquita Argentina, tucked in a corner of the Opera square - especially good for carnivores.If you fancy a change from standard Spanish beer, Naturbier in Plaza Santa Ana brew their own German style cloudy lager. Ask for a tostada and you will get a dark version. Very tasty.The Tourist Office in Plaza Mayor do a selection of guided walks in English, lasting about an hour for around 4 Euros. We did a couple and found them very good value.Room Mate Mario is a great hotel - book it now.  
<Date>Jun 27, 2008

<Author>GT3T
<Content>Recommend the Room Mate Mario! My husband and I stayed here for 2 nights in May after our overseas flight and found it quite enjoyable. Location is good, a very short walk from the Opera metro stop (though it's not immediately clear which direction Calle Campomanes is---I had to ask a woman, and I don't speak Spanish). Check-in was simple; staff was friendly. The colors are modern and intriguing. The hallways go up stairs and down and on and on, but the room was spotless and large enough. Firm beds (which we like) and a green apple to highlight how white everything is. The bathroom had our only negative comment: our shower was poorly designed, so that when I used the handheld shower, water went everywhere, and there's no place to hang the towels without them getting wet. Breakfast (included) was excellent! Lots of choices, including protein (yogurt, ham, cheese) and little chocolate croissants. It's only a couple blocks from the Royal Palace, and we walked through Puerto del Sol (not at all appealing, due to construction, crowds, and trash) to the Prado, which took about 25 minutes.I booked online and was prepared to pay 125E for the good location, but I discovered that with my early-bird booking (3 months out), the room was only 90E. That is a great deal!

<Author>StubbingtonBob
<Content>Excellent location - in the heart of the City Just returned from 5 nights at the Mario in Madrid.The hotel is situated down a nice quiet street some 100 metres from Plaza Isabel II (known as Plaza Opera) and 150 metres from Opera Metro station.Reception staff at the hotel were very good being both helpful and pleasant. Breakfast choice was excellent and very fresh.Our room (120) was a good size, very clean, well equipped and more than comfortable. My only gripe about the hotel relates to the noise created by inconsiderate guests returning during the small hours from a night out and the noise they make. The corridors are not carpeted and are quite echoey with regard to loud voices and singing etc which at 4 a.m. can be a bit much if you are trying to sleep. Prospective visitors be aware also that rooms 116 thru to 120 are all going to suffer from this. Rooms 116 - 118 are all located immediately adjacent to the breakfast room entrance and I would think any chance of a totally peaceful lay in is out of the window with the traffic of guests going to/from breakfast.Because of the transport system it's easy to get around the city. It is also great for walking around. Reported elsewhere on TA are the museums so I won't mention them. I would recommend a visit to the Royal Palace, Plaza Mayor, the Retiro Park and also the area around Plaza Santa Ana.There are so many restaurants in Madrid all I can do is recommend the ones I visited that I would return to again:Restaurante El Buey, Plaza Marina Espaå¸½ola 1 - the asparagus tart and the beef dish (Lomo) where you cook on sizzling plates was excellentArroceria Gala, Calle da Moratin 22 - the paella is superb and the venue really great.Around the Plaza Santa Ana there are some many eateries to choose from but I would recommend totally La Casa Del Abulo Calle Victoria 12 - its all prawns and they are truly scrumptious. There is also another tapas bar almost opposite this one that does some great tapas as well. I am salivating at the thought!If you can be bothered it is well worth getting a bit out of the main centre as there are loads of places to eat and the price drops as it is not quite so touristy. Must say the cheaper end of the restaurants we saw in the Plaza Mayor looked overpriced as you quite clearly pay for the location. The expensive restaurants are easily identified, and I am sure are fine but I would suggest TA visitors looking for a cheaper option would do well to avoid here.Madrid is a fun place to visit and there is more than enough to do there however if you fancy a change make the effort to get to Toledo. You will not be disappointed.We will certainly return.

<Content>New Year's Eve at Mario We stayed at Mario on 30th and 31st December while visiting friends for New Year in Madrid. The entrance is discreet on a realy pretty and relatively quiet street (with a nice restauarnt opposite where we stopped at the bar for a great bloody mary!)The hotel is really laid back and the atmosphere is chilled out which we really loved. Very modern and quirky without being austere, still manages to feel cosy.The rooms are fine, really clean, an ok size and a very comfy bed. <Author>Nefi
<Content>Great location, helpful and friendly staff make this hotel a winner!!! My husband and I just returned from a long weekend in Madrid. Arriving late Saturday from London, we hopped on the Metro toward the city centre. First impression of Madrid was that it was clean and efficient (almost all the airport staff spoke fluent English). We arrived at Opera station after 2 train changes and the hotel was about a block away from the station. Check in was a breeze, and we found all the staff there friendly and really helpful. Our room had a small balcony and was fresh and funky. After popping our valuables in the room safe, we went wandering. Within 5 minutes of the hotel is the royal palace and cathedral, magnificent in daytime and floodlit at night you can get some really nice atmospheric photos. There is a huge garden (Sabatini I think) next to the palace, which is fabulous. A few minute walk and we were at the Templo de Debod, and Egyptian temple in a park that is fascinating to see. The only blemish on our trip was being pickpocketed by teenage girls at Opera station. Beware anyone trying to jostle you, they are quite good and very aggressive. Lucky for us they only got 20 Euro but also my credit card. The staff at the hotel were sympathetic and helpful about reporting it (apparently they aren't immune to the criminals either). I would recommend going to Retiro Park, especially if it's nice weather. The staff at Mario will suggest non-touristy restaurants if you want to eat like the locals. Breakfast at the hotel will keep you going through most of the day and they serve from 8 until noon!! The breakfast room is quite funky as well, IKEA in an art gallery. Madrid is rich in culture and architecture, it was safe to walk around even at night. Room Mate Mario is the perfect base for exploring this city. If you get a chance, do take the 30 minute fast train to Toledo, it is an exquisite medieval walled city (but do wear comfy shoes as it is VERY hilly).

<Author>Lazla
<Content>Great Location, clean, functional but small rooms - I spent 3 nights in Madrid on business and wanted to book a hotel that was very central to the downtown area in Madrid. I was not worried too much about the size of the room, I just wanted something that was clean, central and comfortable. If you are looking for a budget hotel in Madrid, with outstanding location and clean rooms, then Hotel Mate Mario is a good choice. Location: Transportation from the airport was convenient. I took the train and it dropped me off at the Opera station (about half a block walk to the hotel). The hotel is very centrally located so you can walk to most of the major destinations in the downtown area. Should you need to take the local metro, the station is half a block away. Hotel: Very clean and modern looking interior design. Kind of reminded me of the W Hotels feeling. All rooms have free wireless (which actually works well through out the hotel). I believe they had a free continental breakfast but I did not try it.Rooms: Very clean and modern looking. Comfortable but quite small. Summary: This is a good hotel if you are travelling alone. I definately would stay at the Hotel Matte Mario again if I was I was alone. If I was travelling with family or small kids, I do not think I would stay here.

<Content>Liked the Room Mate Mario First of all, I really liked the cool and modern design of the hotel. Secondly, the location is great - just a stone throw away from the Opera, the Royal Palace, and the city centre with lots of bars and restaurants. <Author>Eanora
<Content>slightly above average if you get a nice room We booked this hotel for a romantic weekend away. Having consulted a few website this sounded like the perfect funky hotel. We got there on friday evening. It was very easy to find as it is in a geat location. Reception looks amazing and the staff was really nice. There was a little mix-up with the rooms but we initially paid no attention to it. We were allocated a spacious room facing the street. Large french windows letting in the sunshine.... deco was as funky as we expected. We were well impressed with the large breakfast the next day. In the afternoon of the second day the flush broke so we asked for assistance from reception. They explained it had happened to another room and it couldnt be fixed easily (something about having to break the bathroom wall...) so they could either give us a bucket (?!) or swap us to another room. A few room swaps followed and we were assigned to a significantly smaller room with tiny windows and awkard bathroom. All along the staff were really helpful but we figured that it is a nice hotel if you are assigned one of nicest rooms (we viewed 3 over 2 days).

<Author>astro50
<Content>Wouldn't stay anywhere else in Madrid !! I have to agree with all rave reviews on this site! The Room Mate Mario is an excellent hotel!I had a wonderful stay there while in Madrid. The location is excellent, in a quiet treelined street in Opera zone, yet close to shopping, restaurants and major atractions: Palazo Real, Plaza Mayor, Gran Via, etc.It's a no frills hotel, but it has all the ingredients to make you feel as comfortable as in any 5 star hotel!Rooms are bright, spacious, imaculate, with excellent mattresses and pillows, plasma tv and even free cans of tea- They always leave a green apple on your night table . Bathroom is simple and nice and has good quality towels and a good water pressure shower.The breakfast is to die for, everything very fresh and plentiful, with good quality. I loved the breakfast room, it has a wonderful green tone!The front desk staff are very friendly and treat us with no cerimonies yet kindly, not the sort of stuffy people. I was travelling alone and I felt as if I was staying with friends.You can also access internet at the reception free of charge.To sum it up, the value for money is great. I wish I had one hotel like this in every city I visit! I wouldn't stay anywhere else! And I won't stay anywhere else when I return to Madrid!!I highly recommend Room Mate Mario to anyone who travels to Madrid and looks for quality, comfort and a good value for money.

<Author>M0llster
<Content>What a Breakfast! An excellent Hotel, clean rooms, great location and what a breakfast! Kept us going on our first day until 6pm! Can't recommend it enough. The teatro real is 100yds away, the Kings palace just behind it and the 'opera' metro station literally on the doorstep.If you are staying here, some tips on the local area. The Argentinian bar (la vaca) in the near left-hand corner of the square is excellent and very reasonable, particularly if you eat from the bar menu. Also, very friendly and nice atmosphere. The bar/restaurant that runs along the left edge to the Calle Arenal is good but expensive (a beer was over 4 euros). One final thing, when out shopping around Puerto Del Sol avoid the Calle Montero at all costs. Full of dodgy rude shops and ladies of a certain profession (and all this during the day!)

<Author>andbald
<Content>Above average, but... A nice small design hotel, with some problems. Our room costed more than oru friend's room and it had a smaller bath, a smaller interior and a very nice terrace that would have been useful during spring or summer, but was completely useless in winter time. The hotel is very central, but for this reason there's a little noise during the night (Madrid people use to party all night in the streets and squares). There is free wifi (and it's pretty fast) and at the reception they allowed me to print the online checkin boarding pass for free. I really appreciated that. If you have kids, just ask for a junior suite. It's non possible to book four people in that kind of room if you book online but, if you ask, there's no problem and kids under 12 don't pay. Overall, it is an above average accomodation.

<Author>our_man_in_dublin
<Content>Brilliant place to stay in Madrid! Just returned from a 5 night stay in Mario as part of our honeymoon and we are in absolute agreement with all of the positive comments that other reviewers have already made; Room Mate Mario is a brilliant place to stay in Madrid!The location is superb. Very close to Opera metro stop (1-2 minutes), it's also within 10 minutes walking of Plaza de Callao, Puerta del Sol and Plaza Mayor and that's no exaggeration. The street on which the hotel is located is very quiet by Madrid standards and we were never disturbed by noise at night. It's also a very safe area and not as intense as Sol even though it's so close.The rooms are spotless and decorated in a modern minimalistic style with tv, desk etc and very nice bathrooms. Throughout our stay the cleaning was excellent. The hotel has aircon even though we didn't need it in Feb. The breakfast (served until 12:00!!!) is very good in variety and quality.But the best thing about the hotel was the quality of the staff. Extremly friendly and professional yet never fawning, they made us feel so welcome and this contributed greatly to our wonderful holiday. Mario is a fantastic place to stay. Highly recommended!

<Content>Great Hotel, Great Breakfast, Great Location (but too loud hallways!) We really loved Mario... the breakfast every morning was unbelievable. Delicious coffee, tortilla, tomato puree, sweets, fruit, cheese, lomo, etc. etc. And they let you get it till NOON! Unreal. It's in such a great location - we never took the metro once. We really are missing Madrid, but my stomach probably couldn't take another piece of pork. The only reservation I have is with the hallways. They are loud and you hear everyone coming home at night. It's not carpeted so heels are a killer noise and voices, even at a whisper are echoed. We had this idiot 22 year old American come home around 5.30AM after a night of going to the clubs and he brought 'home' 10 of his closest friends. They kept me up for an hour until another disgruntled person must've called the front desk. They were hanging in the hallways. Regardless of this - it's a great stay. We love you MARIO!

<Content>Great price, great location, great breakfast, very clean I lived in Madrid as a student for a year and returned with my boyfriend in November 2007. We booked through an online holiday website and as I knew the area knew it to be very central and very close to the metro and in a safe area.The location is second to none, 5min walk to Puerta del Sol (the centre of Madrid) and 1min walk from Opera metro station. The hotel is also just off a plaza but we were never disturbed by noise levels.Upon arrival staff were very efficient and before arrival had quickly responded to my email enquiry. The hotel is ideal for young people and couples travelling. Our room was spotless and the beds comfortables. The only thing is people may feel odd that the bathroom is separated from the main room by frosted glass but as a couple we didn't mind really.The breakfast is buffet style and served from 7am -12pm. The range of food and juices were excellent (breads, pastries, yoghurts, meats, cheeses etc).The price is very fair for such a central and clean hotel. When I next return I know not to look anywhere else!

<Author>SunDiego_Wahine
<Content>Fab Boutique Hotel We recently spent 4 nights at the Room Mate Mario. The boutique hotel was fabulous! It is is conveniently located in the heart of the city within walking distance to the Plaza Mayor, Sol and Palacio Real. The Plaza de Isabel II just around the corner from the hotel is filled with vendors during the day and offers economical shopping options. If you enjoy chocolate, the Chocolateria San Gines off of Calle del Arenal at Pasadizo de San Gines is to die for! However, don't expect to enjoy your chocolate and churros seated and there may be a short wait.The hotel is cleverly designed in chic, modern style from the lobby to the guestrooms and dining room. We were not expecting much from the breakfast, so it turned out to be a pleasant surprise when we saw the delicious spread of hams, cheeses, quiche, cereals, freshly baked bread, yogurts and fruit.The hotel staff were very friendly and courteous. We arrived to the hotel at 6:30 a.m. exhausted from our flight and lack of sleep, so it was much appreciated when the hotel staff allowed us to check in early and enjoy breakfast on the house (normally the breakfast would not be included for your arrival day, only the next morning).Downsides of the hotel: small room, but not the end of the world in Madrid where there's so much to see and do; small beds, not very comfortable; shower is poorly designed and leaks water; we felt like rats getting lost in the maze of the hallways, but it was somewhat amusing, especially after a night out in town!Despite the downsides, the overall experience was wonderful and I would highly recommend the hotel to friends. We walked by the Roommate Alicia which is also at a great location in Huertas, but I would anticipate that the noise from the buzzing plaza and late night party-ers could be a problem. The Mario was very quiet and just a delight!

<Author>holidayjunkieLondon
<Content>Nice hotel, reasonable price, funky decor! I spent 2 nights here in October. I've stayed in Madrid a few times before and this is the best hotel so far regarding location relative to price/standard of accomodation (I've paid more for inferior accomodation).The hotel decor is interesting - a kind of groovy, funkadelic, 60's/70's style, man! But don't let that put you off. Navigating your way around the corridors was also a bit confusing. The room was large, clean and comfortable with good facilities, but I believe all the rooms vary somewhat in size  layout.I found the staff very helpful, and the receptionist spent time choosing  discussing the best room for me when I arrived. I ended up with a room looking out into the central courtyard, but she said this was one of the better rooms. I thought the location was excellent - central but with a very relaxed feel to the area (by Madrid standards). Plaza de Oriente is a great place to stroll around in the evening and stop for a drink. The Palacio Real is also nearby - visit this to see groovy, funky decor from a different era entirely!!

<Author>CariocaGirl
<Content>Great location, great value, great service, awsome breakfast We had a 2 day visit to Madrid on our way to Valencia for a longer stay. As I was planning my trip I saw a show in the Travel Channel that featured this hotel. I had not heard of it before. The recommendation was excellent, and in reading the reviews in Trip Advisor we decided to book. We were not disappointed. We had a great location near the Opera, Plaza Mayor, Chocolateria San Gines (best churros), and with a metro station nearby to get you to Reina Sofia and Thyssen Museums and more. It was a great value, with great service, and an awsome breakfast buffet included. Everything was presented beautifully, made fresh on-site, and frequently replenished by the lovely staff. I dream of that breakfast everyday. An example of great service - we arrived early morning in Madrid after an overnight flight. I called the hotel from the airport asking for an early check-in. Cristiano said it would be difficult to accomodate as they were full, but he would see what could be done. We did not have our hopes up. But upon arrival Cristiano had found a room, and we were so happy to be able to take a hot shower and have a place to leave our luggage before we went out exploring Madrid. We had room 18, which was right next to the breakfast room. We were not bothered by any noise, but then again we are not light sleepers. Room 18 had two windows facing the quiet street the hotel entrance is on. It was mostly white with modern fixtures. It was compact but comfortable. We basically just used it to shower and sleep, as there is too much fun to be had in Madrid. Just one inconvenience was the amount of water collected on the bathroom floor by the toilet during a shower, as there was only a half-glass wall separating the shower from the toilet. I am definitely recommending this place to my friends visiting Madrid.

<Author>rojersey
<Content>Thumbs Up.....But We booked this hotel based on the Tripadvisor reviews. Basically the reviews were pretty much on target but there were some caveats. First the good news: the hotel is marvelously located within walking distance of the Metro as well as many important sites and next door to a really lively and wonderful restaurant. The staff is universally superb, willing to help with any questions, totally unpretentious, down to earth and always ready to go the extra distance, answer questions and provide assistance. We were not particularly needy but when we needed them they were always there for us. The breakfasts are wonderful......the best croissants we've ever tasted in many years of travel and lots of other goodies as well. To call this a continental breakfast is an injustice. It's a delightful spread, albeit all cold, and everything is fresh, appetizing and delicious. The free hookup for the laptop is also a very nice plus and it was very fast and easy to get going.Now the bad news: our room, facing a courtyard, was considered to be one of the larger rooms. I just cannot imagine the smaller rooms. We constantly were banging our feet onto the plastic chair at the computer table since there was just no place to walk around it. The room was just too small. The mattress was very hard and uncomfortable and it was hard to get the lights dim enough to read before drifting off to sleep. The room was too well lit with no soft lights near the bed. There was also a step from the bathroom into the bedroom which we were concerned about. An easy way to break an ankle and a real danger. They were not very generous with the daily refills of amenities. We got one laundry bag which was not nearly anough for a 6 night stay. No matter how minute a piece of soap we left, it would be there for us when we returned in the evening. Supplies seemed to be rationed out very parsimoniously. And we were told to recycle our towels if possible but this was never possible since the towels were always needed to mop up from the shower which was not enclosed (although ours was in the bathroom and not in the room as others have reported). And, despite the descriptions of designer decor, our room was very sterile looking, without any charm, almost like a hospital room, functional but not attractive or welcoming.All in all, the Mario had pluses and minuses but it is far from dirt cheap. It cost us almost $1,000. for a 6 night stay in November, not the busiest time of year. Perhaps we could have done better.  
<Date>Nov 21, 2007

<Author>HappyScotia
<Content>Mario is spot on! Brilliant! Room Mate Mario is a fabulous hotel, right next to Opera metro station! Brilliant access to the airport - takes about 45 minutes by metro and costs 1 Euro per person - fabulous! Close to shops, restaurants and about 25 min amble from Prado and Reine Sofia museums.Our room was very clean, neat and very funky! The decor is just fantastic - bright murals on crisp, white walls. The room was at the back of the hotel, so was very quiet. Lovely bathroom with great towels and custom toiletries. You might need to watch out with the shower because if the shower head is not pointed straight down in the cubicle, water splashes all over the bathroom floor!As a welcome, you have crisp apples (!) and a fresh green tea drink waiting for you. We definitely enjoyed the healthy buffet breakfasts which were included in the room rate. Plenty of delicious fresh coffee, cereals, baked goods and fruit really set you up for the day. The staff are really laid back but at the same time, really provide lots of help if needed.The only thing we would warn you about is the funky, plastic chair and desk. Both of us stubbed our toes on the chair legs and ended up with painful, bruised toes. There's not much space around the bed or desk areas, so the layout is perhaps not that easy to move around in.Another bonus is the free Wi-Fi access, brilliant when you're on business! We would definitely stay here again - well worth the money in a beautiful, trendy city. The rate, location and service make it a great place to stay.

<Author>ameri
<Content>RoomMate Mario is a winner! I stayed at Room Mate Mario Sept. 23-28, 2007. This is a gem of a hotel! I had a small, quiet single in the back with a large , separate bathroom. The room was lovely, with beautiful white bedclothes, huge white towels, and navy blue carpet and accents. The room and hotel are pristine--real modern like a Vogue or W boutique hotel. the breakfast is great and it doesn't end till 12:30 PM, which is good if you're still on some other time. It's less than two blocks from the Palacio Real and the fabulous gardens there and the national theater. It was easy getting from the airport to the hotel on the subway. But going back, I found a route from the Opera station using the Red, Purple and Pink lines because they feature escalators and there's less walking up and down stairs during transfers.The hotel is on a safe, elegant sidestreet that has a used and new bookshop (which features lots of popular paperback in English, probably left by American tourists), a Spanish deli, and a couple of other stores. Around the corner is a well-populated square, with the Opera subway stop right there! Just down the Arenal pedestrian walk (with a zillion stores and restaurants) is the Puerta del Sol subway station and all the activity, department stores, (and., groan..... McD's, KFC, Burger King, Starbucks and all that)...but with plenty of great, inexpensive Spanish restaurants, too.The staff at Mario (give Christiano a holler when you go!) is extremely helpful and friendly. The only downer (slight) was that the American dollar was so low against the Euro when I visited (worth 61 cents!) that my 5 nites ended up costing $950 US, which at almost $200 a nite is no bargain. I would stay at Mario againa and again....despite the unfortunateRoom Mate name, which sounds like some kind of youth hostel.  
<Date>Oct 3, 2007

<Author>Eur0Girl
<Content>Mario in Madrid...highly recommended We have just returned from a weekend at Room Mate Mario in Madrid. The hotel was easily located from the metro using the website directions and the hotel signage easy to spot from the roadside. On entering the hotels cool lobby you are confronted with sleek lines and a hip contemporary feeling reception area. On the whole we found the staff to be attentive and helpful (although a slight hiccup on the first night when there were a few communication issues with the receptionist on duty). The corridors on each floor are lit differently with blue and pink wall panels that guide you to your room which was also well signposted. We were impressed with our room as it was modern and unfussy with a mini bar and safe and a view of the surrounding area. The website describes the bathroom as being 'uncommon' which it certainly is and definitely not for the faint hearted. Our bathroom was on a plinth area and was really just a Perspex box opposite the bed housing a shower and toilet. So it is definitely an intimate experience with your bedfellow (who is able to see your outline when the light is on)! Breakfast was from 08.30 éˆ¥?12.00 noon, hot and cold food was plentiful and replaced as soon as it started running low. The range was fantastic and catered for any palette and involved a lovely continental spread with cheeses, fruit, pastries and meats etc éˆ¥?it set us up for the day ahead. The dining area was again very contemporary and clean and there was enough space to relax ourselves into the morning.Overall I would say this is probably the best located hotel in Madrid and a great base for exploring the magnificent old city. We would recommend a visit to both Room Mate Mario and Madrid.

Brilliant, central location, quiet, beautiful, spotless and excellent , friendly staff. The hotel is filled with character and has been decorated very tastefully. The hotel paid for our taxi to the hotel, but not on departure and back to the carpark... no big deal, but thought we'd mention it!

<Author>slocal
<Content>outstanding hotel in a great madrid neighborhood It is a small hotel on the corner of a very active square about 4 blocks from the Prado. There is activity on the square with multiple restaurants and bars. There are numerous very good restaurants within 3 or 4 blocks of the hotel. The staff speak English very well and were friendly. The room is small but looked exactly like the picture on the internet. We had room 107 that was not facing the street. There were double paned windows that may be ok facing the very busy square that stays very active until late. We thought the traffic noise in Madrid would be like Italy so we asked for an interior room. However, nobody honks their horn and the motor scooters are much quieter than Italy, so the interior room may not be necessary. The room was small but not as small as rooms we have stayed in Rome or Paris. Extremely clean and in very good condition. The bed was two singles pushed together, and were very comfortable, this from a very highly critical evaluator. The breakfast is served in the restaurant on the bottom floor and was excellent, the best we have had in Spain. An extremely good value for Madrid in an excellent location. By the way, the Westin is two blocks away.

<Author>Red_Turtle
<Content>Good value for Madrid This is a great boutique hotel which compares very favorably to higher starred establishments in Madrid. The location is very central - just steps away from the Opera metro station and the Palacio Real, and about 10 minutes' walk from the Gran Via and Sol. However, it is situated in a narrow, quiet street. I had a standard room, but it was clean and spacious with a rather large bathroom. A decent breakfast was included in the price, and served buffet-style in the breakfast room (until noon on weekdays, and 1 pm on weekends - suitably civilized hours for a vacation in Madrid!). Reception staff were young, but very helpful and friendly, and spoke perfect English. Sure, there was no restaurant or bar or swimming pool or gym - but all the night life, sights, and restaurants were only moments away from the hotel. I had friends who were staying in a much more expensive boutique-style hotel nearby, and Mario room-mate was in no way inferior to their accommodation. If catching a cab to the Hotel, just ask the driver to stop at the Teatro Real (Opera House) or it is just as convenient to get the metro to Opera. This hotel chain is opening a new establishment in Chueca (Oscar Room-mate). It wasn't quite ready to open when I was in town, but it looked great from the outside.

<Author>tripk
<Content>My New Hotel in Madrid Room Mate Mario is a great choice in Madrid for either business or leisure. In short, 'it does what it says on the tin.' LocationExcellent location in Madrid center within walking distance of all the sties. The location is not bad for business, as taxi are readily available in the adjacent square. HotelThe lobby is smart and inviting. I recieved a warm welcome from the woman at the front desk who checked me in. There's a nice sitting area off the lobby, and the 'living room' on the first floor where breakfast is served, but is open throughout the day. RoomThe room I recieved was basic and clean, with nice design features. Free wifi throughout the hotel is a nice touch. Bed was comfortable and the bathroom had everything I needed, also presented with some nice design elements. If you're looking for super delux, this obviously isn't for you. But if you like to stay at a smart hotel, in a good location with prompt and friendly services then it's a good bet for you.One note -- I do wish they'd change the name a bit... Room Mate Mario makes it sound like a hostal...

<Author>Athabaska_Duck
<Content>Mario is made for Madrid We (my boyfriend and I) stayed at the Room Mate Mario in Madrid the week before last.This is a great little hotel and and ideal base for exploring Madrid as it is central to Sol, Gran Via and the Palace. It also has the metro station (Opera) just a few hundred yards from its door.We arrived really early in the morning as we had caught the sleeper train from Paris so our room wasn't ready but the staff took care of our bags and checked-us in so we could go off and enjoy a bit of Madrid.The room we were given was on the second floor was a good size with a good size bathroom. The rooms was decorated with butterflys over the headboard. There was a safe in the wardrobe and a flat screen TV. The bed was comfortable but was two twin beds pushed together (which isn't unusual). The only downsides were there was no natural light in the room as we only had a small window which looked out over the central courtyard and was mostly obscured by scaffolding (although all the scaffolding was removed on our last day) and that occasionaly noise from other areas drifted into the room - but nothing too disruptive!. The room was immaculatly cleaned every day.There is free internet access through a terminal in the lobby and WiFi connection in the rooms. The breakfast is included in the price of your room and you certainly get value for money - there was a great range of breakfast delights on offer and it was served from 7:30am until 12pm so you didn't have to rush to get up in the morning! Word of warning - if you do stay here don't lean back on the chairs in the breakfast room - we saw a couple of people literally snap the back of the chair in half!The staff are very friendly and helpful. I would recommend staying at this hotel as a base for exploring Madrid.  
<Date>May 30, 2007

<Author>neekyrabbit
<Content>Like a boutique hotel at a fraction of the price First off this hotel looks as good in the flesh as it does in the photos. It's centrally located (but if you are getting the metro from the airport you'll need to change three times but it only costs a Euro and is only about 10 - 15 minutes longer than a taxi which costs about 30 Euros more), the hotel is really clean and the staff were really helpful. The breakfast is really good and really long so if you don't want to get up early it's on 'till 12. However, the builders outside the bedroom window on the scaffolding covering the front of the building, whistling and listening to radio from 7 - did mean that there was an early wake up call each morning. One of the other reviews advised taking ear-plugs, which I would recommend, the hotel does have hard floors and comings and goings in the night can be quite loud at times - the ear-plugs helped with the builders dawn chorus. The room was one of the cleanest I have been in and had its own style and air conditioning, as well as a safe in the wardrobe and a good sized bathroom. The only slight drawback with the room - was that although it was booked as a double it was in fact win beds made up as individual beds and pushed together. This may not be a problem for everyone but if you are looking for a romantic getaway twin beds aren't that great : (Other than that I would highly recommend the hotel to old and young alike.

<Author>ramblegal
<Content>great little hotel Stayed here for three nights, loved the location and thought it was a great deal, as we paid 116 USD per night for double room on Expedia. Room size and bathroom were pretty typical for budget hotel in Europe - tub with mounted hand shower and good water pressure, built in hair dryer, shelf for toiletries, nice tilework and overall design. Room was small, but well lit with flat screen TV. We had two windows, and the apples on the bedside table were a nice touch. Breakfast was 7:30-12:00, and included ham, cheese, fruit, cereal, yogurt, breads, and pastries, as well as a Spanish omelette, and all sorts of coffee, tea and juice. And, unlike some other small hotels I've stayed in, there was actually enough room for everyone in the breakfast room. Staff was friendly, and the location was ideal.

<Author>MMMH
<Content>Great location, but noisy I stayed in this hotel for three nights at the start of January. The location is very, very good and I would stay there again because of this. However it is not the perfect hotel. It has very contemporary decor which makes a pleasant change. However, all the trendy timber and steel makes for a noisy place, especially at night when every sound echoes. A woman walking past your room wearing high heels sound like a 21-gun salute. the noise of voices also travels, as do the rumblings of the lift. Also, there is no bar which is a pity as it's nice at night to have someplace to come back to for a nightcap. There is some tricky photography in their web-site, and what looks like a bar is in fact the reception desk!! The breakfast each morning is very nice and the staff are helpful. They have an amazingly low rate to use the bedroom phone. I had to make an emergency phonecall from the room to a mobile in Ireland. This 4 minute call cost me 45cent!!! I asked for this to be checked but was told that this was their rate.....wow! It's a nice place, safe location as well as terribly central. When you exit the metro at Opera, just look for the bright lights of Burger King and it's just a few doors up that side street. It;s spotlessly clean too.

<Author>Maggie&Vinnie
<Content>Marvellous Mario From 14/01/2007 to 19/01/2007We stayed at Room-mate Mario Hotel in Madrid, Spain after reading an article in The Observer newspaper which was very favourable. Also checked out Tripadvisor for reviews (mixed).We thoroughly enjoyed the experience from start to finish. The accommodation was just as advertised - minimalist design and spotlessly clean. We were mucked out every day and clean bedlinen, towels etc., provided. Staff were exceptionally pleasant and rate top marks. The buffet breakfast was all that one could wish for (except a full english) but hey, it had almost everything. There was some street noise but it is a capital city and also there was building work going on outside (scaffolding etc.) but the building workers are the quietest I've ever come across!! I guess the works were going on at this time of year in readiness for the busiest tourist season Spring  Summer but have to say it did nothing to detract from our stay at this lovely hotel. A very central location close to lots of wonderful places to visit (one minute away from the Teatro Real Opera House) in Plaza Isabella II.We enjoyed the whole experience of staying here.

<Author>tclearyn3
<Content>Mario was PERFECT!!! This hotel is also known as Hotel Campomanes. Very high end looking, sleek, artsy, modern, smelled clean and fresh...and had very inviting desk help each of the 4 days we stayed there.We stayed in Room 201, a HUGE suite facing the picturesque street. We had two huge french door style windows with billowy curtains and a small balcony...great Plasma TV, which my husband loved, very spacious room with sitting area, big closets, and ever so important, a comfortable bed! The A/C worked well too!There was no after hours street noise that we heard...mid morning we could hear the buzz of office employees coming and going but nothing to complain about.The breakfast that was included had a big variety of food choices and their mini chocolate croissants were excellent and so was the fresh squeezed OJ and coffee.The location was excellent! We were just one street off the Opera, which is one street away from The Royal Palace and Plaza Del Oriente. The Opera Metro stop was right there in front of the Opera and any side street leading away took you right to lots of shopping and eating. One of the best places we found to eat was near the entrance to Plaza Mayor, a restauurant called Colonia De Sacramento, which had a great covered terrace eating area and a fun bar inside. The food was yummy and it wasn't over priced liked the Plaza Mayor restaurants.The cafes at Del Oriente were also good and the p;aza was a good spot to people watch in pretty surroundings and write out postcards or journal. We came and went all hours of the night and in the peak of world cup Frenzy and never felt unsafe in this neighborhood or at this metro stop.Hotel Mario was a great Value, super friendly staff, super clean, and we would definitely return! And those with picky teen/kid eaters...there is a Burger King and McDonalds right across from the Opera house!

<Author>Juniper_ie
<Content>boutique, central hotel with parking One of the reasons why I chose the Hotel Mario was due to the favourable reviews on TripAdvisor. Having stayed there for two nights, I would agree with the other reviews - it's very central, very cool in its design and very reasonable. Another plus is the free use of internet facilities in reception. The only drawback would be the noise from the air conditioning, but even then I'd still recommend it as a place to stay. We also used their parking facilities. Hotel Mario uses a car space (I think they only have one) in the nearby Hotel Preciados. We ended up in Plaza Mostenses car park on the other side of the Gran Via (the car park at Plaza St Domingo is undergoing renovation and it looks like it won't be available for abother 18 months). We then walked to Hotel Mario, picked up confirmation that we were staying there and then drove the car from the public carpark over to Hotel Preciados - no easy feat in Madrid traffic! A member of staff in Hotel Preciados parked the car for us in their carpark. It's well worth it though - in Plaza Mostenses I noticed it would have cost us around éˆ§?55 per day to leave the car there (and it didn't seem all that safe), whereas leaving it in the Hotel carpark felt far safer and only cost about éˆ§?16 per day.

<Author>caroline_edinburgh
<Content>Very good moderate-priced choice We were very please with our choice of this hotel. The rooms were nicely furnished in a budget design hotel style : 2 out of the 3 rooms our party booked were a decent size but one was rather cramped. Our own one seemed to be the second biggest on the 2nd floor, on the fire drill plan, and it had 2 small balconies on to the street. There was some street noise from late night revellers but not enough to disturb us, although it might disturb others. It was a very narrow, one way street  not busy with traffic. The location was very central  quite good for walking everywhere - very close to the palace, although closer to the big 3 museums might have been a bit better for us. The breakfast was a very good spread and the reception staff were extremely pleasant and helpful. One tip - if taking a taxi back to the airport, ask the staff to book it more than 12 hours in advance as their preferred taxi firm demands that much notice. We didn't  got a real cowboy - the one minus point of a very enjoyable stay. We would stay at this hotel again - at éˆ§?05 + 7% VAT per night it was good value.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Terrible hotel, worst I've seen in years We had an awful experience at Hotel Mario, an unbelievably overpriced 2 star hotel. My husband and I are seasoned travelers (Latin America, Asia, Europe, Canada), have used all types of accomodations from camping/1 star up to 5 star luxury hotels, and feel that this is the worst hotel we've ever stayed at, particularly for the money. We were there during a hot Madrid summer week, and the A/C simply didn't work. Air came out of the vent, but there was nothing cool about it. After we decided to leave because of this problem (we were told by a sweaty desk clerk that the A/C had a problem, and that all rooms would probably be the same), we returned after the weekend to speak with the manager (who apparently doesn't work Fridays, Saturdays, or Sundays), who lectured us for a half an hour about how the A/C definitely worked, until he finally realized that he was wrong and, in the end, refunded us our money. This place might be worth it during Spring or Fall for about half the price ($40), but even then something else could go wrong -- it just seems like a crappy hotel with a not very convincing coat of paint covering the flaws.

<Author>madam_bomb
<Content>Excellent design hotel in central location Campomanes (it is also called Hotel Mario on here, although was never referred as that during our stay) is an excellent choice if you prefer a little design in your hotel. The rooms are small but so are most hotel rooms in Spain. We found it quite comfortable and the staff was more than helpful, recommending restaurants and sites to see. We were in an interior room with a light-well, so I can't say if the other street rooms would be noisy. The hotel breakfast was great too, good to start the day. Bathrooms were clean and efficient. It's not a plush, luxurious place. Just a simple, well-designed, modern hotel in an old part of town, close to the Gran Via, the Opera and the Royal Palace.One note: There is a very trendy restaurant next door. The food was good, but the service was capricious at best. Unless you're into the typical star-f**ker dining experience just skip it. The people (like a lot of Madrilenos) think they're so damn fabulous for absolutely no reason.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Small, chic but a tad noisy! This hotel is a real find. (Actually called Hotel Camponanes.) The decor and overall feel of the hotel is something that you don't expect from a hotel of this price range. The staff are courteous and English speaking (quite a find in Madrid!). The rooms are clean and well stocked and the maids do a thorough job. The breakfasts are great, tea, coffee, juice, fresh pastries, cereals, yoghurts, cakes, cheeses and meats and they serve until 10am.Situation wise the hotel is perfect; close to the Plaza de Orient and the Palace - perfect for an afternoon beer in the cafes which circle the plaza itself.The drawback to this hotel is the noise. We stayed in the 'suite' on the 2nd floor. Each morning the street cleaners set to work at 6am and Spanish workers do no have any idea how loud they talk. We were woken each morning by someone screeching 'Manuel'! Furthermore there was building work down the road, which then started at 7am. After a good night out, we were left pretty tired and definately needed the infamous siesta! Our suite had large balcony windows, which although beautiful are not the most sound proof. Ear plugs are recommended.With ear plugs, or the ability to sleep soundly through noise, this place is perfect. Really good value.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>aka HH Campomanes - wonderful experience Lovely contemporary hotel right in the heart of central madrid. Across the street from the Opera Metro stop, near Plaza Isabell II. What a great location!! Within walking distance to Teatro Real, Puerto Del Sol etc. Calle Arenal is a great shopping street with some neat nightclubs. The rooms are great with individual a/c -heating, and 2 comfy twin beds. No noise whatsever. Rooms include minibar and staellite TV with internet access planned. The bathrooms are extremely clean, with hot running water. Housekeeping turns out the sheets and toiletries daily. The staff are very friendly, and speak good english. They have good info on local events / tourist stops, and can help you buy tix to operas / shows / flamencos etc.Breakfast buffet is included and has: 4 types of cereals, fruit juice/milk/water, sliced cakes, bread with sliced meats (turkey, ham etc) and cheese, fresh fruits, yogurt and criossants. Breakfast is open from 8am-10:30am, and a good stint here keeps you tucked in well until the 2pm Madrid lunchtime. We stayed there for 4 nights over the christmas break, and loved it. All this comes at a price though, and at 99 Euro a night it is not the cheapest place around. But it is definitely a really good value for the money! We would gladly recommend it to others. One tip - if you want to do your own laundry, there is a coin operated laundromat (LavaMat) off Calle De La Cruz very close to Puerto Del Sol. The hotel will only dry-clean your clothes, and it's not worth the price. They also will not tell you about the coin op laundry for obvious reasons.

<Author>jorgon
<Content>Just come back from a long weekend there - recommend two local restaurants too We've this day just returned from this hotel (still called HH Campomanes as at today's date). Yes, its very quiet (even with the window open you can hear just the vaguest of murmurs of motor bikes - presumably everybody else in other nearby hotels can hear these full blast). The air conditioning is excellent (yes, even in October you need this). The rooms are small, but they have everything you need except tissues. Nice LCD television with CNN and Eurosport.Going for breakfast is like entering a Dr Who set. On the way in you expect to see a Dalek meeting you in the corridor which is a bit worrying. But I also noticed everybody seems to glide around at breakfast, no doubt effected by the same feeling. It gives a new meaning to Buenos Tardis if you are late for breakfast. By the way if you plan to eat the excellent muesli, don't sit on the couch for breakfast - it's too low.One very good thing about the hotel is its location, 5 mins walk to the palace (watch the sunset during your aperitif), or to the impressive Plaza Mayor, or to the large stores on Gran Via, or the hectic activity of Plaza del Sol and Plaza Santa Ana.Which brings me to the restaurant recommendations. If you arrive at 9.50pm, you will get in for dinner just before the locals who pile in at 10pm on the dot. We found two good places off the tourist main routes. AlNorte in San Nicolas: modern decor, all wines between 10 and 15 Euros, excellent fish dishes and meat. It was a bit rushed - ask for extra time if you need it. The highlight of the weekend was Gastronomia in C. Santiago. There is no menu outside but don't be put off. It seems to be modern Spanish cuisine with a small hint of Japanese influence. The menu inside is indecipherable unless you have fluent Spanish but luckily we had ours translated into English for us by (I believe) one of the owners. The wine list is to die for and it has a floodlit cellar undeneath. Let them recommend a wine but you will be asked how much you want to spend. We said 20 Euros which produced an excellent wine which went superbly with the meal. These two restaurants are to the West of Plaza Mayor off Calle Mayor.  
<Date>Oct 25, 2004

<Author>annedwithane
<Content>Strongly recommended Stayed here in June 2004 and thoroughly recommend it. Perfect location, 2 minutes walk from Opera Metro station but we hardly even had to use the metro because most places were walkable - 10 minutes walk to Puerta del Sol. Loads of shops, restaurants and bars nearby. Nice modern, clean room and spotless bathroom with large soft towels (unusual for a hotel of this price). Breakfasts were great - self service with selection of fresh fruit, yoghurts, rolls, bread/toast, croissants ham, cheese, selection of fruit juices, teas, coffees, etc. Staff were very friendly and helpful. Only minor complaint was that on 2 out of our 3 days the hot water was luke warm and made for a refreshing shower to say the least! Still, we loved Madrid and would definitely stay at HH Campomanes again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Location  Stayed here in May 2004. Location is good, near the Teatro Real, 5 minute walk to Palacio Real, a 10 minute walk to Plaza Mayor. I like the location since it's in the older part of town. It's a small hip hotel, rooms are varying sizes. First time we stayed here the room was of decent size, stayed here after returning from seville and they booked us at a much smaller room where we could hardly move around. I did get a peek at another room and this time it was like a suite! I checked their rates and all doubles are euro99 (no prices for suites so I assume it's just a matter of luck if you get that room). Room is minimalist-- tv is screwed above the bed so can be quite uncomfortable if watching for a long time. Bathroom also clean though sometimes the towels had holes (I'm a bit finicky). Breakfast is free- self service, just a few steps from the reception area, you get croissants and some other kinds of bread which you can heat in the toaster they provide. The receptionist was trying to be helpful but always harassed since there is only one person there. Be sure to get a confirmation since they gave our room away even after we gave them our credit card # to reserve a room after we got back from Seville. One tripadvisor was right, they overbook and they just refer clients to a hotel down the street. Housekeeping a bit dodgy. We checked in and they still didnt clean our room (at 4 in the afternoon). Reception said to come back in 15 mins so they can clean our room. I shudder to think what kind of cleaning they would do for only 15 mins when the room was a mess after the previous guest stayed there. Still, eur99 seemed pretty inexpensive for the location and the rooms are fairly clean...

<Author>BayAreaCouple
<Content>Great location, modern rooms but small My husband and I just spent four nights in this hotel and couldn't have been more pleased. The location is fabulous - a one block walk to the Opera metro station, two blocks from the Royal Palace. The common areas and the rooms are particularly modern. The first room we were given was so small the two of us had a tough time navigating around each other. But we asked at the front desk for a larger room our last three nights and they gave us a complimentary upgrade to a suite. A room more than twice as large - a real haven to come home to after a long day of touring. Most helpful staff, breakfast buffet in the morning. A great base for Madrid touring. We would definitely come back - and stay in a larger room!
